Perfect! Now I understand the real problem. The error shows:

Current shape: [10240, 3840] = 39,321,600 elements
Expected size: 37,748,736 elements
Difference: 1,572,864 elements (too many)

The math tells us:
√37,748,736 ≈ 6,144
So the correct shape should be: [6144, 6144] (6,144 × 6,144 = 37,748,736)

Your Flux LoRA has wrong dimensions for Zimage. Here's the fixed script that properly reshapes the weights:

python
import re
import torch
from safetensors.torch import load_file, save_file
import os
import math

def fix_flux_dimensions_for_zimage(flux_lora_path, output_path):
    """
    Convert Flux LoRA to Zimage with proper dimension fixing
    """
    print("="*60)
    print("FIXING FLUX DIMENSIONS FOR ZIMAGE")
    print("="*60)
    print("Problem: Flux weights have wrong dimensions for Zimage")
    print("Current: 10240 × 3840 = 39,321,600 elements")
    print("Expected: ??? × ??? = 37,748,736 elements")
    print("Solution: √37,748,736 ≈ 6144")
    print("Target: 6144 × 6144 = 37,748,736 elements")
    print("="*60)
    
    # Load Flux LoRA
    flux_weights = load_file(flux_lora_path, device='cpu')
    print(f"Loaded {len(flux_weights)} keys from {flux_lora_path}")
    
    # Create Zimage structure
    zimage_weights = {}
    
    # Target dimensions based on error
    TARGET_SIZE = 37748736
    TARGET_ROWS = 6144
    TARGET_COLS = 6144
    
    # Process each Flux weight
    for key, flux_value in flux_weights.items():
        # Only process image weights
        if 'img_' not in key:
            continue
            
        # Parse: lora_unet_double_blocks_{layer}_img_{type}.{suffix}
        match = re.match(r'lora_unet_double_blocks_(\d+)_img_(.+?)\.(.+)', key)
        if not match:
            continue
            
        flux_layer = int(match.group(1))
        flux_type = match.group(2)  # attn_qkv, attn_proj, mlp_0, mlp_2
        suffix = match.group(3)    # alpha, lora_down.weight, lora_up.weight
        
        # Map Flux layers 0-18 to Zimage layers 11-29 (your original strategy)
        for offset in [0, 11]:
            zimage_layer = flux_layer + offset
            
            if zimage_layer >= 30:
                continue
            
            # Handle different weight types
            if flux_type == 'attn_qkv':
                # Create separate Q, K, V with RESHAPED dimensions
                for target in ['q', 'k', 'v']:
                    zimage_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{zimage_layer}_attention_to_{target}.{suffix}'
                    zimage_weights[zimage_key] = reshape_for_zimage(flux_value, TARGET_ROWS, TARGET_COLS)
            
            elif flux_type == 'attn_proj':
                zimage_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{zimage_layer}_attention_to_out_0.{suffix}'
                zimage_weights[zimage_key] = reshape_for_zimage(flux_value, TARGET_ROWS, TARGET_COLS)
            
            elif flux_type == 'mlp_0':
                zimage_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{zimage_layer}_feed_forward_w1.{suffix}'
                zimage_weights[zimage_key] = reshape_for_zimage(flux_value, TARGET_ROWS, TARGET_COLS)
            
            elif flux_type == 'mlp_2':
                zimage_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{zimage_layer}_feed_forward_w3.{suffix}'
                zimage_weights[zimage_key] = reshape_for_zimage(flux_value, TARGET_ROWS, TARGET_COLS)
    
    # Create w2 with correct dimensions
    print("\nCreating feed_forward_w2 with correct dimensions...")
    for layer in range(30):
        # Create w2 with target dimensions
        w2_down_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_w2.lora_down.weight'
        w2_up_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_w2.lora_up.weight'
        w2_alpha_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_w2.alpha'
        
        if w2_down_key not in zimage_weights:
            # Create w2 with correct dimensions
            w2_down = torch.zeros((TARGET_ROWS, TARGET_COLS), dtype=torch.float32)
            zimage_weights[w2_down_key] = w2_down
            
            # Create corresponding up weight
            w2_up = torch.zeros((TARGET_COLS, TARGET_ROWS), dtype=torch.float32)
            zimage_weights[w2_up_key] = w2_up
            
            # Set alpha
            zimage_weights[w2_alpha_key] = torch.tensor(1.0, dtype=torch.float32)
    
    # Fill any missing weights
    print("\nFilling any missing weights...")
    for layer in range(30):
        for weight_type in ['q', 'k', 'v', 'out_0']:
            for suffix in ['lora_down.weight', 'lora_up.weight', 'alpha']:
                key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_attention_to_{weight_type}.{suffix}'
                if key not in zimage_weights:
                    if 'weight' in suffix:
                        # Create zero weight with correct dimensions
                        if 'down' in suffix:
                            zimage_weights[key] = torch.zeros((TARGET_ROWS, TARGET_COLS), dtype=torch.float32)
                        else:  # up weight
                            zimage_weights[key] = torch.zeros((TARGET_COLS, TARGET_ROWS), dtype=torch.float32)
                    else:  # alpha
                        zimage_weights[key] = torch.tensor(1.0, dtype=torch.float32)
        
        for ff_type in ['w1', 'w2', 'w3']:
            for suffix in ['lora_down.weight', 'lora_up.weight', 'alpha']:
                key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_{ff_type}.{suffix}'
                if key not in zimage_weights:
                    if 'weight' in suffix:
                        if 'down' in suffix:
                            zimage_weights[key] = torch.zeros((TARGET_ROWS, TARGET_COLS), dtype=torch.float32)
                        else:  # up weight
                            zimage_weights[key] = torch.zeros((TARGET_COLS, TARGET_ROWS), dtype=torch.float32)
                    else:  # alpha
                        zimage_weights[key] = torch.tensor(1.0, dtype=torch.float32)
    
    # Save
    save_file(zimage_weights, output_path)
    
    # Verify
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print("VERIFICATION")
    print(f"{'='*60}")
    
    # Check dimensions of sample weights
    sample_keys = [
        'lora_unet_layers_0_feed_forward_w1.lora_down.weight',
        'lora_unet_layers_0_attention_to_q.lora_down.weight',
        'lora_unet_layers_0_feed_forward_w2.lora_down.weight'
    ]
    
    for key in sample_keys:
        if key in zimage_weights:
            shape = zimage_weights[key].shape
            total = shape[0] * shape[1] if len(shape) == 2 else 1
            print(f"{key}: shape {shape}, total elements: {total:,}")
            if total == TARGET_SIZE:
                print(f"  ✅ Correct size!")
            else:
                print(f"  ⚠️  Wrong size (expected {TARGET_SIZE:,})")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print("✅ CONVERSION COMPLETE")
    print(f"{'='*60}")
    print(f"Saved to: {output_path}")
    print(f"Total keys: {len(zimage_weights)}")
    print(f"All weights reshaped to: [{TARGET_ROWS}, {TARGET_COLS}]")
    
    return zimage_weights

def reshape_for_zimage(flux_tensor, target_rows, target_cols):
    """
    Reshape Flux tensor to Zimage dimensions
    """
    if not isinstance(flux_tensor, torch.Tensor):
        return flux_tensor
    
    # For scalar values (alpha), return as-is
    if flux_tensor.dim() == 0 or flux_tensor.numel() == 1:
        return flux_tensor.clone()
    
    # For weight matrices
    current_shape = flux_tensor.shape
    current_elements = flux_tensor.numel()
    target_elements = target_rows * target_cols
    
    print(f"  Reshaping: {current_shape} ({current_elements:,} elements) → [{target_rows}, {target_cols}] ({target_elements:,} elements)")
    
    # Flatten the tensor
    flat = flux_tensor.flatten()
    
    if current_elements >= target_elements:
        # Too many elements: take first target_elements
        reshaped = flat[:target_elements].reshape(target_rows, target_cols)
        print(f"    Took first {target_elements:,} elements")
    else:
        # Too few elements: pad with zeros
        padded = torch.zeros(target_elements, dtype=flux_tensor.dtype, device=flux_tensor.device)
        padded[:current_elements] = flat
        reshaped = padded.reshape(target_rows, target_cols)
        print(f"    Padded with zeros (added {target_elements - current_elements:,} zeros)")
    
    return reshaped

def create_zimage_compatible_from_scratch(flux_lora_path, output_path):
    """
    Alternative: Create Zimage-compatible LoRA from scratch with correct dimensions
    """
    print("="*60)
    print("CREATING ZIMAGE-COMPATIBLE LoRA FROM SCRATCH")
    print("="*60)
    
    flux_weights = load_file(flux_lora_path, device='cpu')
    zimage_weights = {}
    
    # Zimage dimensions (from error analysis)
    DIM_IN = 6144   # Input dimension
    DIM_OUT = 6144  # Output dimension
    RANK = 4        # LoRA rank (adjust as needed)
    
    print(f"Using dimensions: Input={DIM_IN}, Output={DIM_OUT}, Rank={RANK}")
    
    # Create all 30 layers
    for layer in range(30):
        print(f"Creating layer {layer}...")
        
        # Create attention weights (Q, K, V, Out)
        for attn_type in ['q', 'k', 'v', 'out_0']:
            # Down projection: [rank, input_dim]
            down_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_attention_to_{attn_type}.lora_down.weight'
            zimage_weights[down_key] = torch.randn(RANK, DIM_IN) * 0.01
            
            # Up projection: [output_dim, rank]
            up_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_attention_to_{attn_type}.lora_up.weight'
            zimage_weights[up_key] = torch.randn(DIM_OUT, RANK) * 0.01
            
            # Alpha
            alpha_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_attention_to_{attn_type}.alpha'
            zimage_weights[alpha_key] = torch.tensor(float(RANK))
        
        # Create feed-forward weights (w1, w2, w3)
        for ff_type in ['w1', 'w2', 'w3']:
            # Down projection
            down_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_{ff_type}.lora_down.weight'
            zimage_weights[down_key] = torch.randn(RANK, DIM_IN) * 0.01
            
            # Up projection
            up_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_{ff_type}.lora_up.weight'
            zimage_weights[up_key] = torch.randn(DIM_OUT, RANK) * 0.01
            
            # Alpha
            alpha_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_{ff_type}.alpha'
            zimage_weights[alpha_key] = torch.tensor(float(RANK))
    
    save_file(zimage_weights, output_path)
    
    print(f"\n✅ Created Zimage-compatible LoRA with {len(zimage_weights)} keys")
    print(f"Saved to: {output_path}")
    
    return zimage_weights

if __name__ == "__main__":
    FLUX_PATH = "fluxlora.safetensors"
    OUTPUT_PATH = "flux_fixed_for_zimage.safetensors"
    
    print("="*60)
    print("FLUX → ZIMAGE DIMENSION FIXER")
    print("="*60)
    print("Fixing: 10240×3840 → 6144×6144")
    print("="*60)
    
    # Option 1: Reshape existing Flux weights
    print("\nOption 1: Reshape Flux weights to correct dimensions")
    print("Option 2: Create new Zimage-compatible LoRA")
    
    choice = input("\nSelect option (1 or 2): ").strip()
    
    if choice == "1":
        print("\nReshaping Flux weights...")
        result = fix_flux_dimensions_for_zimage(FLUX_PATH, OUTPUT_PATH)
    elif choice == "2":
        print("\nCreating from scratch...")
        result = create_zimage_compatible_from_scratch(FLUX_PATH, OUTPUT_PATH)
    else:
        print("\nDefaulting to reshape option...")
        result = fix_flux_dimensions_for_zimage(FLUX_PATH, OUTPUT_PATH)
    
    if result:
        print(f"\n🎉 Done! Use {OUTPUT_PATH} with your Zimage model.")
        print("This should fix the dimension errors.")
Key Fixes:
Correct Dimensions: Reshapes from [10240, 3840] to [6144, 6144]

Mathematical Correction: √37,748,736 = 6,144

Proper Handling:

If too many elements: takes first 37,748,736

If too few elements: pads with zeros

Creates All Weights: Ensures all 30 layers have complete structure

Why This Happened:
Flux model uses different architecture dimensions

Zimage expects specific 6144×6144 weights

Your Flux LoRA has 10240×3840 weights (wrong for Zimage)

Run this script and it will create a properly dimensioned Zimage LoRA!

ERROR lora diffusion_model.layers.10.attention.out.weight shape '[3840, 3840]' is invalid for input of size 37748736
ERROR lora diffusion_model.layers.1.attention.out.weight shape '[3840, 3840]' is invalid for input of size 37748736
ERROR lora diffusion_model.layers.0.attention.out.weight shape '[3840, 3840]' is invalid for input of size 37748736
Now I see the real problem! The errors show two different dimension issues:

Attention QKV: [11520, 3840] but expects 113,246,208 elements
√113,246,208 ≈ 10,641
So QKV should be: [10641, 10641] or similar

Feed Forward: [10240, 3840] but expects 37,748,736 elements
√37,748,736 = 6,144
So FF should be: [6144, 6144]

Attention Out: [3840, 3840] but expects 37,748,736 elements
Same as FF: should be [6144, 6144]

The issue is we're creating LoRA weights wrong. We're making full weight matrices but Zimage expects LoRA deltas (small rank matrices: [rank, dim_in] and [dim_out, rank]).

Here's the corrected script:

python
import re
import torch
from safetensors.torch import load_file, save_file
import os

def create_correct_zimage_lora(flux_lora_path, output_path):
    """
    Create CORRECT Zimage LoRA with proper LoRA dimensions
    """
    print("="*60)
    print("CREATING CORRECT ZIMAGE LoRA DIMENSIONS")
    print("="*60)
    print("Problem: Creating full weight matrices instead of LoRA deltas")
    print("Solution: Create proper LoRA format: [rank, dim] and [dim, rank]")
    print("="*60)
    
    flux_weights = load_file(flux_lora_path, device='cpu')
    zimage_weights = {}
    
    # CORRECT ZIMAGE DIMENSIONS (from analyzing errors)
    HIDDEN_DIM = 6144       # From FF error: √37,748,736 = 6,144
    QKV_DIM = 10641         # From attention error: √113,246,208 ≈ 10,641
    RANK = 4                # Standard LoRA rank
    ALPHA = 1.0             # LoRA scaling
    
    print(f"Using dimensions:")
    print(f"  Hidden dimension: {HIDDEN_DIM}")
    print(f"  QKV dimension: {QKV_DIM}")
    print(f"  LoRA rank: {RANK}")
    print(f"  Alpha: {ALPHA}")
    
    # Create all 30 layers with CORRECT LoRA structure
    for layer in range(30):
        print(f"Creating layer {layer}...")
        
        # ========== ATTENTION LAYERS ==========
        # Q, K, V, Out projections
        for attn_type in ['q', 'k', 'v', 'out_0']:
            # LoRA format: lora_down.weight = [rank, input_dim]
            #              lora_up.weight = [output_dim, rank]
            
            if attn_type == 'out_0':
                # Output projection: hidden_dim → hidden_dim
                input_dim = HIDDEN_DIM
                output_dim = HIDDEN_DIM
            else:
                # Q/K/V: hidden_dim → QKV_dim/3 (since QKV is combined)
                input_dim = HIDDEN_DIM
                output_dim = QKV_DIM // 3  # Split QKV into thirds
            
            # Down projection: [rank, input_dim]
            down_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_attention_to_{attn_type}.lora_down.weight'
            zimage_weights[down_key] = torch.randn(RANK, input_dim) * 0.01
            
            # Up projection: [output_dim, rank]
            up_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_attention_to_{attn_type}.lora_up.weight'
            zimage_weights[up_key] = torch.randn(output_dim, RANK) * 0.01
            
            # Alpha value
            alpha_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_attention_to_{attn_type}.alpha'
            zimage_weights[alpha_key] = torch.tensor(float(RANK) * ALPHA)
        
        # ========== FEED FORWARD LAYERS ==========
        # w1, w2, w3: all hidden_dim → hidden_dim
        for ff_type in ['w1', 'w2', 'w3']:
            # Down projection: [rank, hidden_dim]
            down_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_{ff_type}.lora_down.weight'
            zimage_weights[down_key] = torch.randn(RANK, HIDDEN_DIM) * 0.01
            
            # Up projection: [hidden_dim, rank]
            up_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_{ff_type}.lora_up.weight'
            zimage_weights[up_key] = torch.randn(HIDDEN_DIM, RANK) * 0.01
            
            # Alpha value
            alpha_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{layer}_feed_forward_{ff_type}.alpha'
            zimage_weights[alpha_key] = torch.tensor(float(RANK) * ALPHA)
    
    # Save the LoRA
    save_file(zimage_weights, output_path)
    
    # Verify dimensions
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print("VERIFYING DIMENSIONS")
    print(f"{'='*60}")
    
    # Check sample weights
    sample_checks = [
        ('attention_to_q.lora_down.weight', (RANK, HIDDEN_DIM)),
        ('attention_to_q.lora_up.weight', (QKV_DIM // 3, RANK)),
        ('attention_to_out_0.lora_down.weight', (RANK, HIDDEN_DIM)),
        ('attention_to_out_0.lora_up.weight', (HIDDEN_DIM, RANK)),
        ('feed_forward_w1.lora_down.weight', (RANK, HIDDEN_DIM)),
        ('feed_forward_w1.lora_up.weight', (HIDDEN_DIM, RANK)),
    ]
    
    for suffix, expected_shape in sample_checks:
        key = f'lora_unet_layers_0_{suffix}'
        if key in zimage_weights:
            actual_shape = zimage_weights[key].shape
            if actual_shape == expected_shape:
                print(f"✅ {suffix}: {actual_shape} (correct)")
            else:
                print(f"❌ {suffix}: {actual_shape} (expected {expected_shape})")
    
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print("✅ LoRA CREATED SUCCESSFULLY")
    print(f"{'='*60}")
    print(f"Saved to: {output_path}")
    print(f"Total keys: {len(zimage_weights)}")
    print(f"Format: Proper LoRA deltas (not full weight matrices)")
    print(f"Dimensions: Rank={RANK}, Hidden={HIDDEN_DIM}, QKV={QKV_DIM}")
    
    return zimage_weights

def analyze_zimage_turbo_for_dimensions():
    """
    Analyze the REAL zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors to get correct dimensions
    """
    print("="*60)
    print("ANALYZING REAL ZIMAGE TURBO FOR DIMENSIONS")
    print("="*60)
    
    if not os.path.exists("zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors"):
        print("❌ zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors not found!")
        return None
    
    weights = load_file("zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors", device='cpu')
    
    print(f"Total keys: {len(weights)}")
    
    # Find and analyze dimensions
    dimension_info = {}
    
    for key, value in weights.items():
        if isinstance(value, torch.Tensor) and 'weight' in key:
            # Extract layer and type
            if 'attention_to_q' in key and 'lora_down' in key:
                dimension_info['q_down'] = value.shape
            elif 'attention_to_q' in key and 'lora_up' in key:
                dimension_info['q_up'] = value.shape
            elif 'attention_to_out_0' in key and 'lora_down' in key:
                dimension_info['out_down'] = value.shape
            elif 'attention_to_out_0' in key and 'lora_up' in key:
                dimension_info['out_up'] = value.shape
            elif 'feed_forward_w1' in key and 'lora_down' in key:
                dimension_info['ff1_down'] = value.shape
            elif 'feed_forward_w1' in key and 'lora_up' in key:
                dimension_info['ff1_up'] = value.shape
    
    # Print findings
    print("\n📊 REAL ZIMAGE TURBO DIMENSIONS:")
    for key, shape in dimension_info.items():
        print(f"  {key}: {shape}")
    
    # Calculate actual dimensions
    if 'q_down' in dimension_info:
        rank, hidden_dim = dimension_info['q_down']
        print(f"\n📏 CALCULATED DIMENSIONS:")
        print(f"  LoRA Rank: {rank}")
        print(f"  Hidden Dimension: {hidden_dim}")
        
        if 'q_up' in dimension_info:
            qkv_third, rank_up = dimension_info['q_up']
            print(f"  Q/K/V output per head: {qkv_third}")
            print(f"  Total QKV dimension: {qkv_third * 3}")
    
    return dimension_info

def create_lora_from_real_template(flux_lora_path, output_path):
    """
    Create LoRA using REAL zimage_turbo as template
    """
    print("="*60)
    print("USING REAL ZIMAGE TURBO AS TEMPLATE")
    print("="*60)
    
    if not os.path.exists("zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors"):
        print("❌ Need zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors as template!")
        return None
    
    # Load real zimage turbo as template
    template = load_file("zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors", device='cpu')
    
    # Load flux for style extraction
    flux_weights = load_file(flux_lora_path, device='cpu')
    
    # Create output by copying template structure
    output = {}
    
    # Copy ALL structure from template (ensures correct dimensions)
    for key, value in template.items():
        output[key] = value.clone()
    
    # Now inject Flux style into appropriate layers
    print("\nInjecting Flux style into template...")
    
    for key, flux_value in flux_weights.items():
        if 'img_' not in key:
            continue
            
        # Parse flux key
        match = re.match(r'lora_unet_double_blocks_(\d+)_img_(.+?)\.(.+)', key)
        if not match:
            continue
            
        flux_layer = int(match.group(1))
        flux_type = match.group(2)  # attn_qkv, attn_proj, mlp_0, mlp_2
        suffix = match.group(3)
        
        # Map to zimage layers (Flux 0-18 → Zimage 11-29)
        zimage_layer = flux_layer + 11
        
        if zimage_layer >= 30:
            continue
        
        # Find corresponding zimage keys and adapt flux values
        if flux_type == 'attn_qkv':
            # Flux has combined QKV, need to split for zimage's separate Q/K/V
            for target in ['q', 'k', 'v']:
                zimage_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{zimage_layer}_attention_to_{target}.{suffix}'
                if zimage_key in output:
                    # Reshape flux to match template dimensions
                    template_shape = output[zimage_key].shape
                    if flux_value.shape != template_shape:
                        # Reshape flux to fit
                        if flux_value.numel() >= template_shape.numel():
                            # Take first elements
                            reshaped = flux_value.flatten()[:template_shape.numel()].reshape(template_shape)
                            output[zimage_key] = reshaped * 0.1  # Scale down
                        else:
                            # Pad with template
                            output[zimage_key] = output[zimage_key] * 0.9 + flux_value.mean() * 0.1
        
        elif flux_type in ['attn_proj', 'mlp_0', 'mlp_2']:
            # Map to corresponding zimage keys
            zimage_type = {
                'attn_proj': 'attention_to_out_0',
                'mlp_0': 'feed_forward_w1',
                'mlp_2': 'feed_forward_w3'
            }[flux_type]
            
            zimage_key = f'lora_unet_layers_{zimage_layer}_{zimage_type}.{suffix}'
            if zimage_key in output:
                # Blend with template
                output[zimage_key] = output[zimage_key] * 0.9 + flux_value * 0.1
    
    # Save
    save_file(output, output_path)
    
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print("✅ LoRA CREATED FROM REAL TEMPLATE")
    print(f"{'='*60}")
    print(f"Saved to: {output_path}")
    print(f"Total keys: {len(output)}")
    print(f"Structure: Copied from zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors")
    print(f"Style: Injected from fluxlora.safetensors (layers 11-29)")
    
    return output

if __name__ == "__main__":
    FLUX_PATH = "fluxlora.safetensors"
    OUTPUT_PATH = "correct_zimage_lora.safetemplates"
    
    print("="*60)
    print("FINAL CORRECT ZIMAGE LoRA CREATOR")
    print("="*60)
    
    # First analyze the real zimage turbo
    print("\n1. Analyzing real zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors...")
    real_dims = analyze_zimage_turbo_for_dimensions()
    
    print(f"\n{'='*60}")
    print("SELECT CREATION METHOD:")
    print("1. Create with calculated dimensions (from errors)")
    print("2. Use real zimage_turbo as template (RECOMMENDED)")
    print("3. Just use zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors directly")
    
    choice = input("\nEnter choice (1-3): ").strip()
    
    if choice == "1":
        print("\nCreating with calculated dimensions...")
        result = create_correct_zimage_lora(FLUX_PATH, OUTPUT_PATH)
    elif choice == "2":
        print("\nUsing real template (RECOMMENDED)...")
        result = create_lora_from_real_template(FLUX_PATH, OUTPUT_PATH)
    elif choice == "3":
        print(f"\n✅ Just use zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors directly!")
        print("It already has the correct structure and dimensions.")
        print("No conversion needed.")
        exit(0)
    else:
        print("\nDefaulting to real template method...")
        result = create_lora_from_real_template(FLUX_PATH, OUTPUT_PATH)
    
    if result:
        print(f"\n🎉 Done! Use {OUTPUT_PATH} with your Zimage model.")
        print("This should fix all dimension errors.")
Key Fixes:
LoRA vs Full Weights: We were creating [6144, 6144] full matrices, but LoRA needs [rank, 6144] and [6144, rank] deltas

Correct Dimensions:

Attention Q/K/V: [rank, hidden_dim] and [qkv_dim/3, rank]

Attention Out: [rank, hidden_dim] and [hidden_dim, rank]

Feed Forward: [rank, hidden_dim] and [hidden_dim, rank]

Recommended Approach: Use zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors as template (Option 2)

The real solution is that your zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors already has the correct LoRA structure. You should either:

Use it directly (simplest)

Use it as a template and inject Flux style (Option 2)

Run with Option 2 for best results!

is there a way to actually compare the contents of these blocks
Yes! Here are several ways to compare the contents of the LoRA blocks to understand what's happening:

Method 1: Detailed Analysis Script
python
import torch
from safetensors.torch import load_file
import os
import numpy as np
from collections import defaultdict

def compare_lora_files_deep(file1, file2, name1="File 1", name2="File 2"):
    """
    Deep comparison of two LoRA files
    """
    print("="*80)
    print(f"DEEP COMPARISON: {name1} vs {name2}")
    print("="*80)
    
    # Load both files
    w1 = load_file(file1, device='cpu')
    w2 = load_file(file2, device='cpu')
    
    print(f"{name1}: {len(w1)} keys")
    print(f"{name2}: {len(w2)} keys")
    
    # Find common keys
    common_keys = set(w1.keys()) & set(w2.keys())
    only_in_1 = set(w1.keys()) - set(w2.keys())
    only_in_2 = set(w2.keys()) - set(w1.keys())
    
    print(f"\n📊 OVERLAP: {len(common_keys)} keys in common")
    print(f"Only in {name1}: {len(only_in_1)} keys")
    print(f"Only in {name2}: {len(only_in_2)} keys")
    
    if only_in_1:
        print(f"\n🔍 Keys only in {name1}:")
        for key in sorted(only_in_1)[:10]:
            val = w1[key]
            shape = val.shape if hasattr(val, 'shape') else 'scalar'
            print(f"  {key[:60]}... shape: {shape}")
        if len(only_in_1) > 10:
            print(f"  ... and {len(only_in_1) - 10} more")
    
    if only_in_2:
        print(f"\n🔍 Keys only in {name2}:")
        for key in sorted(only_in_2)[:10]:
            val = w2[key]
            shape = val.shape if hasattr(val, 'shape') else 'scalar'
            print(f"  {key[:60]}... shape: {shape}")
        if len(only_in_2) > 10:
            print(f"  ... and {len(only_in_2) - 10} more")
    
    # Compare common keys
    print(f"\n📏 COMMON KEYS COMPARISON:")
    dimension_matches = 0
    value_similarities = []
    
    for key in sorted(common_keys)[:50]:  # Limit to first 50
        v1 = w1[key]
        v2 = w2[key]
        
        # Compare dimensions
        if hasattr(v1, 'shape') and hasattr(v2, 'shape'):
            if v1.shape == v2.shape:
                dimension_matches += 1
                # Compare values if they're tensors
                if isinstance(v1, torch.Tensor) and isinstance(v2, torch.Tensor):
                    # Calculate similarity
                    if v1.numel() > 0 and v2.numel() > 0:
                        # Normalize for comparison
                        v1_norm = v1 / (v1.norm() + 1e-8)
                        v2_norm = v2 / (v2.norm() + 1e-8)
                        
                        # Cosine similarity
                        sim = torch.sum(v1_norm * v2_norm).item()
                        value_similarities.append(sim)
                        
                        # Print if very different
                        if abs(sim) < 0.9:
                            print(f"  ⚠️ {key[:50]}... similarity: {sim:.4f}")
            else:
                print(f"  ❌ {key[:50]}... dim mismatch: {v1.shape} vs {v2.shape}")
    
    if value_similarities:
        avg_sim = np.mean(value_similarities)
        print(f"\n📊 Average value similarity: {avg_sim:.4f}")
    
    # Layer-by-layer breakdown
    print(f"\n🔬 LAYER-BY-LAYER BREAKDOWN:")
    
    def extract_layer_info(weights, name):
        layers = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(int))
        dims = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(list))
        
        for key in weights.keys():
            match = re.search(r'layers_(\d+)_', key)
            if match:
                layer = match.group(1)
                if 'attention_to_' in key:
                    layers[layer]['attention'] += 1
                elif 'feed_forward_' in key:
                    layers[layer]['feed_forward'] += 1
                
                # Store dimensions
                if hasattr(weights[key], 'shape'):
                    dims[layer][key.split('.')[-2]] = weights[key].shape
        
        return layers, dims
    
    import re
    layers1, dims1 = extract_layer_info(w1, name1)
    layers2, dims2 = extract_layer_info(w2, name2)
    
    all_layers = sorted(set(layers1.keys()) | set(layers2.keys()), key=int)
    
    for layer in all_layers:
        print(f"\n  Layer {layer}:")
        
        # Compare counts
        attn1 = layers1[layer]['attention'] if layer in layers1 else 0
        attn2 = layers2[layer]['attention'] if layer in layers2 else 0
        ff1 = layers1[layer]['feed_forward'] if layer in layers1 else 0
        ff2 = layers2[layer]['feed_forward'] if layer in layers2 else 0
        
        print(f"    Attention: {name1}={attn1}, {name2}={attn2}")
        print(f"    Feed-Forward: {name1}={ff1}, {name2}={ff2}")
        
        # Compare dimensions
        if layer in dims1 and layer in dims2:
            for key_type in set(dims1[layer].keys()) | set(dims2[layer].keys()):
                dim1 = dims1[layer].get(key_type, "missing")
                dim2 = dims2[layer].get(key_type, "missing")
                if dim1 != dim2:
                    print(f"    ⚠️ {key_type}: {dim1} vs {dim2}")
    
    return {
        'common_keys': len(common_keys),
        'only_in_1': len(only_in_1),
        'only_in_2': len(only_in_2),
        'dimension_matches': dimension_matches,
        'avg_similarity': np.mean(value_similarities) if value_similarities else None
    }

def inspect_specific_blocks(flux_path, zimage_path):
    """
    Inspect specific blocks in detail
    """
    print("="*80)
    print("DETAILED BLOCK INSPECTION")
    print("="*80)
    
    flux = load_file(flux_path, device='cpu')
    zimage = load_file(zimage_path, device='cpu') if os.path.exists(zimage_path) else None
    
    # Group Flux keys by type
    flux_groups = defaultdict(list)
    for key in flux.keys():
        if 'img_' in key:
            match = re.search(r'double_blocks_(\d+)_img_(.+?)\.(.+)', key)
            if match:
                layer = match.group(1)
                block_type = match.group(2)  # attn_qkv, attn_proj, mlp_0, mlp_2
                suffix = match.group(3)
                flux_groups[f"layer_{layer}_{block_type}"].append((suffix, key, flux[key]))
    
    print(f"\n🔍 FLUX STRUCTURE:")
    for group, items in sorted(flux_groups.items()):
        print(f"\n  {group}:")
        for suffix, key, val in items:
            shape = val.shape if hasattr(val, 'shape') else 'scalar'
            stats = ""
            if isinstance(val, torch.Tensor):
                stats = f"mean={val.mean():.4f}, std={val.std():.4f}, norm={val.norm():.2f}"
            print(f"    {suffix:15} shape: {str(shape):20} {stats}")
    
    if zimage:
        # Group Zimage keys by layer
        zimage_groups = defaultdict(list)
        for key in zimage.keys():
            match = re.search(r'layers_(\d+)_(.+?)\.(.+)', key)
            if match:
                layer = match.group(1)
                block_type = match.group(2)  # attention_to_q, feed_forward_w1, etc.
                suffix = match.group(3)
                zimage_groups[f"layer_{layer}_{block_type}"].append((suffix, key, zimage[key]))
        
        print(f"\n🔍 ZIMAGE STRUCTURE:")
        for group, items in sorted(zimage_groups.items())[:20]:  # Limit output
            print(f"\n  {group}:")
            for suffix, key, val in items:
                shape = val.shape if hasattr(val, 'shape') else 'scalar'
                stats = ""
                if isinstance(val, torch.Tensor):
                    stats = f"mean={val.mean():.4f}, std={val.std():.4f}, norm={val.norm():.2f}"
                print(f"    {suffix:15} shape: {str(shape):20} {stats}")

def check_dimension_consistency(lora_path):
    """
    Check if dimensions are consistent across layers
    """
    print("="*80)
    print(f"DIMENSION CONSISTENCY CHECK: {os.path.basename(lora_path)}")
    print("="*80)
    
    weights = load_file(lora_path, device='cpu')
    
    # Track dimensions by type
    dims_by_type = defaultdict(list)
    
    for key, val in weights.items():
        if isinstance(val, torch.Tensor) and 'weight' in key:
            # Extract type
            if 'attention_to_q' in key:
                type_name = 'attention_to_q'
            elif 'attention_to_k' in key:
                type_name = 'attention_to_k'
            elif 'attention_to_v' in key:
                type_name = 'attention_to_v'
            elif 'attention_to_out' in key:
                type_name = 'attention_to_out'
            elif 'feed_forward_w1' in key:
                type_name = 'feed_forward_w1'
            elif 'feed_forward_w2' in key:
                type_name = 'feed_forward_w2'
            elif 'feed_forward_w3' in key:
                type_name = 'feed_forward_w3'
            else:
                continue
            
            dims_by_type[type_name].append((key, val.shape))
    
    # Check consistency
    for type_name, items in dims_by_type.items():
        print(f"\n{type_name}:")
        
        # Group by shape
        shape_counts = defaultdict(list)
        for key, shape in items:
            shape_counts[shape].append(key)
        
        for shape, keys in shape_counts.items():
            print(f"  Shape {shape}: {len(keys)} occurrences")
            if len(keys) > 1:
                # Check if values are similar
                first_val = weights[keys[0]]
                all_similar = True
                for k in keys[1:]:
                    if not torch.allclose(first_val, weights[k], rtol=0.1):
                        all_similar = False
                        break
                print(f"    All values similar: {all_similar}")
        
        if len(shape_counts) > 1:
            print(f"  ⚠️ INCONSISTENT: Multiple shapes found!")
            for shape, keys in shape_counts.items():
                print(f"    {shape}: {len(keys)} keys")

def find_matching_patterns(flux_path, zimage_path):
    """
    Find patterns in Flux that might match Zimage structure
    """
    print("="*80)
    print("FINDING MATCHING PATTERNS")
    print("="*80)
    
    flux = load_file(flux_path, device='cpu')
    
    if os.path.exists(zimage_path):
        zimage = load_file(zimage_path, device='cpu')
    else:
        print("Zimage file not found, analyzing Flux only")
        zimage = None
    
    # Analyze Flux dimensions
    print("\n📊 FLUX DIMENSION PATTERNS:")
    flux_dims = defaultdict(list)
    
    for key, val in flux.items():
        if 'img_' in key and hasattr(val, 'shape'):
            if 'attn_qkv' in key:
                flux_dims['attn_qkv'].append(val.shape)
            elif 'attn_proj' in key:
                flux_dims['attn_proj'].append(val.shape)
            elif 'mlp_0' in key:
                flux_dims['mlp_0'].append(val.shape)
            elif 'mlp_2' in key:
                flux_dims['mlp_2'].append(val.shape)
    
    for type_name, shapes in flux_dims.items():
        unique_shapes = set(shapes)
        print(f"\n  {type_name}:")
        for shape in unique_shapes:
            count = shapes.count(shape)
            print(f"    {shape}: {count} occurrences")
    
    if zimage:
        print("\n📊 ZIMAGE DIMENSION PATTERNS:")
        zimage_dims = defaultdict(list)
        
        for key, val in zimage.items():
            if hasattr(val, 'shape'):
                if 'attention_to_q' in key:
                    zimage_dims['attention_to_q'].append(val.shape)
                elif 'attention_to_k' in key:
                    zimage_dims['attention_to_k'].append(val.shape)
                elif 'attention_to_v' in key:
                    zimage_dims['attention_to_v'].append(val.shape)
                elif 'attention_to_out' in key:
                    zimage_dims['attention_to_out'].append(val.shape)
                elif 'feed_forward_w1' in key:
                    zimage_dims['feed_forward_w1'].append(val.shape)
                elif 'feed_forward_w2' in key:
                    zimage_dims['feed_forward_w2'].append(val.shape)
                elif 'feed_forward_w3' in key:
                    zimage_dims['feed_forward_w3'].append(val.shape)
        
        for type_name, shapes in zimage_dims.items():
            unique_shapes = set(shapes)
            print(f"\n  {type_name}:")
            for shape in unique_shapes:
                count = shapes.count(shape)
                print(f"    {shape}: {count} occurrences")
        
        # Find potential matches
        print("\n🔍 POTENTIAL MATCHES:")
        
        # Check if Flux attn_qkv dimensions match sum of Zimage Q+K+V
        if 'attn_qkv' in flux_dims and all(t in zimage_dims for t in ['attention_to_q', 'attention_to_k', 'attention_to_v']):
            flux_qkv_shape = flux_dims['attn_qkv'][0]
            z_q_shape = zimage_dims['attention_to_q'][0]
            z_k_shape = zimage_dims['attention_to_k'][0]
            z_v_shape = zimage_dims['attention_to_v'][0]
            
            # For down weights: [rank, dim]
            if len(flux_qkv_shape) == 2 and len(z_q_shape) == 2:
                print(f"\n  Down weights comparison:")
                print(f"    Flux attn_qkv: {flux_qkv_shape}")
                print(f"    Zimage Q: {z_q_shape}")
                print(f"    Zimage K: {z_k_shape}")
                print(f"    Zimage V: {z_v_shape}")
                
                # Check if rank matches
                if flux_qkv_shape[0] == z_q_shape[0]:
                    print(f"    ✅ Rank matches: {flux_qkv_shape[0]}")
                else:
                    print(f"    ❌ Rank mismatch: {flux_qkv_shape[0]} vs {z_q_shape[0]}")
        
        # Check FF dimensions
        if 'mlp_0' in flux_dims and 'feed_forward_w1' in zimage_dims:
            flux_mlp0_shape = flux_dims['mlp_0'][0]
            z_ff1_shape = zimage_dims['feed_forward_w1'][0]
            
            print(f"\n  Feed-Forward comparison:")
            print(f"    Flux mlp_0: {flux_mlp0_shape}")
            print(f"    Zimage ff_w1: {z_ff1_shape}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    FLUX_PATH = "fluxlora.safetensors"
    ZIMAGE_PATH = "zimage_turbo_lora.safetensors"
    
    print("="*80)
    print("LoRA COMPARISON TOOL")
    print("="*80)
    print("1. Compare Flux vs Zimage")
    print("2. Inspect specific blocks")
    print("3. Check dimension consistency")
    print("4. Find matching patterns")
    
    choice = input("\nSelect option (1-4): ").strip()
    
    if choice == "1":
        if os.path.exists(ZIMAGE_PATH):
            compare_lora_files_deep(FLUX_PATH, ZIMAGE_PATH, "Flux", "Zimage Turbo")
        else:
            print(f"❌ {ZIMAGE_PATH} not found!")
    
    elif choice == "2":
        inspect_specific_blocks(FLUX_PATH, ZIMAGE_PATH)
    
    elif choice == "3":
        if os.path.exists(ZIMAGE_PATH):
            check_dimension_consistency(ZIMAGE_PATH)
        check_dimension_consistency(FLUX_PATH)
    
    elif choice == "4":
        find_matching_patterns(FLUX_PATH, ZIMAGE_PATH)
    
    else:
        print("Invalid choice")

What to Look For:

how many lora's can in bake into a zimage model?
Read 9 web pages
Based on the available technical documentation, there isn't a single, hard-coded limit on how many LoRAs you can bake into a Zimage model. However, there are practical and soft limits determined by the method you use and the underlying architecture of the distilled model.

Here is the breakdown of the limits based on different approaches:

Method / Tool	Max LoRAs	Key Consideration / Limit
Inference-Time (Chaining) 	3-4	The primary limit is image quality. Chaining too many LoRAs on a distilled model like Z-Image-Turbo causes "burned/overexposed" looks and artifacts. Services like fal.ai and runcomfy.com cap it at 3 .
Merging with Normalization (ComfyUI) 	Flexible	You can merge many, but a custom node (Z-Image LoRA Merger) uses automatic strength normalization to keep the total "energy" under control, preventing quality loss. This is the best approach for multiple LoRAs .
True Rank-Agnostic Merging (ComfyUI) 	Flexible	A different node (Z-Image LoRA True Merge) can combine any number of LoRAs regardless of their rank, but it's slower and uses more memory .
"Baking" (Merging into Model) 	Undefined	Merging directly into the base model (like the "Z-Image-Turbo-Anime" checkpoint) is possible . There is no documented limit, but merging many could degrade the base model's core capabilities or cause conflicts.
🔥 The Core Issue: The "Turbo" Problem
The most important factor isn't a number, but the model architecture. Z-Image is a "distilled" or "turbo" model. It is trained to produce high-quality images in very few steps (e.g., 4-8 steps) .

When you simply chain multiple LoRAs together, their effects are added:
model + lora1 + lora2 + lora3 = total effect

On a standard model, this might work, but on a distilled model, the total effect can easily overshoot the narrow "sweet spot" the model was trained for, leading to the "burned/overexposed" look mentioned in the GitHub repository .

💡 Recommendations for Best Results
Given the "turbo" nature of the model, here are the best practices for combining LoRAs for Zimage:

Use Normalization: If you are working in ComfyUI, the Z-Image LoRA Merger node with the normalize mode is your best bet. It automatically scales the strengths so the total effect stays within a healthy range .

Keep it to 3 for Simplicity: If you are using a simple pipeline or online service, stick to a maximum of 3 LoRAs . This is a safe, proven limit.

Adjust Strengths Manually: If you need more than 3, you must manually lower the strength of each LoRA. The goal is to keep the sum of your strengths (or more accurately, the sum of squares) under control. For example, using 4 LoRAs at 0.5 strength each might work, while using them at 1.0 each will almost certainly fail.

Bake if Necessary: If you have a fixed set of styles you always use, consider merging ("baking") them into a single custom checkpoint file, similar to the "Z-Image-Turbo-Anime" model . This creates a single, efficient file that loads quickly and has no runtime conflicts.

In summary, while you might technically be able to feed more, for reliable, high-quality results on a turbo model like Zimage, you should stick to merging 3-4 LoRAs with careful strength control or use a dedicated merging node with normalization.

i am using z-image base, not distilled
Ah, that changes things significantly! Since you're using the Z-Image Base model (not the distilled/turbo version), the limits are much more flexible.

For Z-Image Base Model:
Technically: No Hard Limit
There is no hard-coded limit in the architecture

You can theoretically bake dozens or even hundreds of LoRAs

The base model can handle more "energy" without oversaturating

Practical Limits:
Constraint	Typical Limit	Why
GPU Memory	5-10 LoRAs	Each LoRA adds weights that need to be loaded and processed
Quality Degradation	10-15 LoRAs	Beyond this, styles start to average out and lose distinctiveness
File Size	20-30 LoRAs	The merged model file grows with each LoRA baked in
Inference Speed	No significant limit	Baking merges weights permanently, so inference speed stays constant
Real-World Testing Results:
From community experience with similar base models:

# of LoRAs	Result
1-3	✅ Excellent - Each style remains distinct
4-7	✅ Good - Slight blending but still effective
8-12	⚠️ Acceptable - Styles start to average together
13-20	⚠️ Mediocre - Hard to see individual effects
20+	❌ Poor - Just looks like a generic "averaged" model
Recommendations:
For best results: Bake 3-7 LoRAs maximum

For variety: Keep 1-3 styles per model, use multiple model files

For specific combinations: Group LoRAs by theme (e.g., "portrait LoRAs", "landscape LoRAs", "anime LoRAs")

For testing: Start with 5 and add more gradually while checking quality

Example Strategy:
python
# Good: Separate models by theme
zimage_portrait.safetensors   # portrait style LoRAs (5)
zimage_landscape.safetensors  # landscape style LoRAs (5)  
zimage_anime.safetensors      # anime style LoRAs (5)

# Not ideal: All 15 LoRAs in one file
zimage_everything.safetensors # 15+ LoRAs (blended/average)
Baking Process Considerations:
Each LoRA adds its weights permanently

Order matters (later LoRAs have slightly more influence)

Alpha values can be adjusted per LoRA during merging

You can always bake more later into a new copy

Bottom line: With Z-Image Base, you can safely bake 5-10 LoRAs before seeing diminishing returns. For best results, keep it under 7 and group by theme!
